## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology / mathematical biology (population dynamics ODEs)
**Analysis**: The target is a time derivative of population size, dP_dt, as a function of time t and population P, which is the standard setup for ecological growth models written as ordinary differential equations. Typical relationships encode per-capita growth, density dependence (carrying capacity), Allee effects at low density, and time-varying (seasonal) growth rates.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Constant net change: dP_dt = c0 (immigration/emigration dominated change independent of P)
- Linear (affine) growth law: dP_dt = c0 + c1 * P (baseline influx plus proportional reproduction/death)
- Exponential/Malthusian growth ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P (constant per-capita growth rate)
- Power-law per-capita scaling: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 (nonlinear reproduction or aggregation effects)
- Logistic growth ODE (Verhulst): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (density dependence with carrying capacity-like saturation)
- Generalized (theta) logistic ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (flexible density dependence; c2 tunes approach to carrying capacity)
- Gompertz growth ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (per-capita growth decreases ~ log(P); tumor/microbial/forest stand growth)
- Richards growth ODE (generalized logistic): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2)**c3 (asymmetric sigmoids via shape parameter c3)
- Allee effect (strong) with carrying capacity: dP_dt = c0 * P * (c1 * P - 1) * (1 - c2 * P) (negative growth at low P; two nonzero equilibria)
- Harvesting/removal (constant yield): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 (fishing/harvest independent of P)
- Harvesting/removal (proportional): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 * P (mortality/harvest proportional to population)
- Seasonally forced per-capita growth: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t + c3)) * P (periodic environment affecting intrinsic growth)
- Time-varying carrying capacity (environmental forcing): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 + c2 * sin(c3 * t)) * P) (seasonal resources change effective density dependence)
- Autonomous polynomial density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**2 - c2 * P**3 (higher-order crowding/competition terms)
- Externally driven trend in growth rate: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * t) * P (slowly changing environment causing secular change in per-capita growth)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Per-capita growth identification: (dP_dt) / P being approximately constant suggests dP_dt ≈ c0 * P (exponential growth/decline).
- Carrying capacity signature: dP_dt crossing zero at a positive P and becoming negative for larger P suggests a factor like (1 - c1 * P) or (1 - (c1 * P)**c2).
- Strength of density dependence: if dP_dt falls roughly linearly with P at large P, quadratic crowding (−c * P**2) is plausible; faster-than-linear decline suggests higher powers (−c * P**m, m>2).
- Allee effect signature: negative dP_dt at small positive P but positive dP_dt at intermediate P implies an additional low-density factor like (c * P - 1).
- Asymmetric sigmoidal approach: if growth slows early and then more sharply near capacity, log terms (Gompertz) or Richards-type exponents often fit better than simple logistic.
- Seasonality detection: oscillations in dP_dt at similar P values across time suggest coefficients that are sinusoidal in t, e.g., (c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t + c3)) multiplying P or P*(1-cP).
- Harvesting fingerprint: a vertical shift downward in dP_dt vs P (even at P≈0) suggests constant-yield removal (−c0), while slope reduction suggests proportional removal (−c * P).
- Finite-time blow-up risk: if dP_dt grows faster than linearly with P (superlinear P**c with c>1) without negative feedback, trajectories may accelerate unrealistically—often indicating missing density dependence terms.
- Time-trend forcing: systematic drift in dP_dt over t at comparable P indicates r(t) changes (e.g., c0 + c1 * t) rather than purely P-dependent dynamics.

- Term 1: `P*exp(negative*t)` — exponential decay times P
- Term 2: `P²/(linear in P)` — a rational function of P

Let me check candidates systematically.

**Candidate 6:** `P*c0 + P*c1/(P + c2) + P**c3*c4 + P**c5*c6*exp(c7*t)`

Setting c5=1: `P*c0 + P*c1/(P+c2) + P**c3*c4 + P*c6*exp(c7*t)`

This gives the exponential term. Now `P*c1/(P+c2)` — can this equal `P²/(c4*P+c5)`? We have `P*c1/(P+c2) = c1*P/(P+c2)`. The GT term is `0.3156*P²/(9.871P+1)`. These aren't the same form.

But wait: `P**c3*c4` with c3=2 gives `c4*P²`. Combined with `P*c0`: total non-exp, non-rational terms are `c0*P + c4*P²`. The rational part is `c1*P/(P+c2)`. We need `c0*P + c4*P² + c1*P/(P+c2) = 0.3156*P²/(9.871P+1)`. This doesn't simplify nicely.

**Candidate 39:** `P*c0 + P*c1/(P + c2) + P*c3*exp(c4*t)`

This gives: `c0*P + c1*P/(P+c2) + c3*P*exp(c4*t)`. The exp term matches with c4=-0.0541, c3=0.3156. Now: `c0*P + c1*P/(P+c2)` needs to equal `0.3156*P²/(9.871P+1)`.

`c0*P + c1*P/(P+c2) = P[c0 + c1/(P+c2)] = P[(c0*P + c0*c2 + c1)/(P+c2)]`

We need this to equal `0.3156*P²/(9.871P+1)`. So: `P*(c0*P + c0*c2 + c1)/(P+c2) = 0.3156*P²/(9.871P+1)`.

Matching denominators: `P+c2` corresponds to `9.871P+1`, so c2 = 1/9.871 (after scaling). Actually, `9.871P+1 = 9.871(P + 1/9.871)`. So set c2 = 1/9.871.

Then numerator: `c0*P + c0*c2 + c1` must equal `0.3156*P/9.871 = 0.03197*P`.

This means: coefficient of P: c0 = 0.03197, and constant: c0*c2 + c1 = 0, so c1 = -c0*c2 = -0.03197/9.871 = -0.003238.

Let me verify: `P*(0.03197*P + 0)/(P + 0.1013) = 0.03197*P²/(P + 0.1013)`

And GT: `0.3156*P²/(9.871P+1) = 0.3156*P²/[9.871(P+0.1013)] = 0.03197*P²/(P+0.1013)` ✓

So candidate 39 works with:
- c0 = 0.03197
- c1 = -0.003238
- c2 = 0.1013
- c3 = 0.3156
- c4 = -0.0541

This is a perfect match!

**The GT has basis functions: {P*exp(-αt), P²/(βP+γ)}**

The term P²/(βP+γ) can also be written as P/β - γP/(β(βP+γ)) = P/β - γ/(β²) + γ²/(β²(βP+γ)).

So GT = c0*P*exp(-c1*t) + c2*P²/(c4*P+c5) which can be expanded as:
GT = c0*P*exp(-c1*t) + (c2/c4)*P - c2*c5/(c4*(c4*P+c5))
= c0*P*exp(-c1*t) + (c2/c4)*P - (c2*c5/c4²) + c2*c5²/(c4²*(c4*P+c5))

So GT can be written as: A*P*exp(-αt) + B*P + C + D/(eP+f)

Or equivalently: A*P*exp(-αt) + B*P + C*P/(P+d)

Let me verify: P*c/(P+d) = cP/(P+d). And P²/(aP+b) = (1/a)*P²/(P+b/a). 

We can write P²/(P+d) = P - d + d²/(P+d). So P²/(aP+b) = (1/a)[P²/(P+b/a)] = (1/a)[P - b/a + b²/(a²(P+b/a))].

Now let me check candidates that could match:

**Candidate 39: P*c0 + P*c1/(P+c2) + P*c3*exp(c4*t)**

This has: linear P, P/(P+c2), P*exp(c4*t).
P*c1/(P+c2) is NOT the same as P²/(P+c2). We need P²/(aP+b), which requires a P² term or P*P/(P+c) form.

Wait - P*c1/(P+c2) ≠ c1*P²/(P+c2). Let me re-read: it's P*c1/(P+c2) = c1*P/(P+c2).

But GT needs P²/(aP+b). Can we get P² from the combination? 
GT = A*P*exp(-αt) + B*P²/(βP+1)

Rewrite B*P²/(βP+1) = (B/β)*P - (B/β²) + (B/β²)/(βP+1) ... no wait:
B*P²/(βP+1): let me do polynomial division. P²/(βP+1) = P/β - 1/β² + (1/β²)/(βP+1).

So GT = A*P*exp(-αt) + (B/β)*P - B/β² + B/(β²(βP+1))

This is: P*exp(-αt) term + P term + constant + 1/(linear in P) term.

Now Candidate 39: c0*P + c1*P/(P+c2) + c3*P*exp(c4*t)
= c0*P + c1*P/(P+c2) + c3*P*exp(c4*t)

c1*P/(P+c2) = c1 - c1*c2/(P+c2)

So = c3*P*exp(c4*t) + (c0+c1)*P - c1 + ... wait, that's wrong.
c1*P/(P+c2) = c1[1 - c2/(P+c2)] = c1 - c1*c2/(P+c2)

So Candidate 39 = c3*P*exp(c4*t) + c0*P + c1 - c1*c2/(P+c2)

GT expanded = A*P*exp(-αt) + (B/β)*P - B/β² + B/(β²(βP+1))

Matching:
- P*exp(t): c4 = -α ✓
- P term: c0 = B/β ✓
- constant: c1 = -B/β² ... but then -c1*c2/(P+c2) must equal B/(β²(βP+1))

From constant: c1 = -B/β²
Then -c1*c2/(P+c2) = (B/β²)*c2/(P+c2)

We need this = B/(β²(βP+1)) = (B/β²) * 1/(βP+1)

So c2/(P+c2) = 1/(βP+1)? That means c2/(P+c2) = 1/(βP+1).
Cross multiply: c2*(βP+1) = P+c2 → c2*β*P + c2 = P + c2 → c2*β = 1 → c2 = 1/β.

Then 1/(βP+1) = c2/(P+c2) = (1/β)/(P+1/β) = 1/(βP+1) ✓

So Candidate 39 MATCHES! Let me verify with actual numbers.

GT: 0.3156*P*exp(-0.0541*t) + 0.3156*P²/(9.871*P+1)

β = 9.871, B = 0.3156
B/β = 0.03197, B/β² = 0.003239

Candidate 39: c0*P + c1*P/(P+c2) + c3*P*exp(c4*t)
c3 = 0.3156 (A), c4 = -0.0541
c0 = B/β = 0.03197
c1 = -B/β² = -0.003239
c2 = 1/β = 0.10131

Check: c0*P + c1*P/(P+c2) = 0.03197*P + (-0.003239)*P/(P+0.10131)
= 0.03197*P - 0.003239*P/(P+0.10131)

Common denominator: [0.03197*P*(P+0.10131) - 0.003239*P]/(P+0.10131)
= P*[0.03197*P + 0.03197*0.10131 - 0.003239]/(P+0.10131)
= P*[0.03197*P + 0.003239 - 0.003239]/(P+0.10131)
= 0.03197*P²/(P+0.10131)
= 0.3156*P²/(9.871*P + 1) ... let me verify: 0.03197*P²/(P+0.10131) = 0.03197*P²/(P+0.10131)

Multiply num and denom by 9.871: = 0.3156*P²/(9.871P + 1.0000) ✓

**Candidate 39 is a MATCH!**

Now let me check **Candidate 41: P*c0 + P*c1/(P+c2) + P*c3*exp(c4*t) + P*c5**

This is the same as Candidate 39 but with an extra P*c5 term. Set c5=0 → same as 39. MATCH.

**Candidate 14: P²*c0 + P*c1 + P*c2/(P+c3) + P*c4*exp(c5*t) + P*c6**

Extra P² term and extra P terms. We can set c0=0 to eliminate P², then it becomes like Candidate 41. MATCH.

Let me now systematically go through all candidates.

**Candidate 6: P*c0 + P*c1/(P+c2) + P^c3*c4 + P^c5*c6*exp(c7*t)**

GT = P*exp(-αt) term + P²/(βP+1) term.

We need P^c5*c6*exp(c7*t) = A*P*exp(-αt), so c5=1, c7=-α.
Then P*c0 + P*c1/(P+c2) + P^c3*c4 must equal P²/(βP+1).

From above, P*c0 + P*c1/(P+c2) can produce P²/(βP+1) (as shown for Candidate 39).
Then set c4=0 to eliminate P^c3 term. MATCH.

Wait, but can we also use P^c3*c4 to help? Actually, setting c4=0 is simplest. Then it reduces to Candidate 39 form. MATCH.

**Candidate 60: P*c0 + P*c1/(P+c2) + P^c3*c4 + P^c5*c6*exp(c7*t) + c8**

Same as Candidate 6 with extra constant c8. Set c4=0, c8=0 → Candidate 39. MATCH.

**Candidate 17: P*c0 + P*c1/(P+c2) + P*c3*(P*c4)^c5 + P*c6*exp(c7*t) + P*c8**

P*c3*(P*c4)^c5 = c3*c4^c5 * P^(1+c5). Set c3=0 to eliminate. Then P*c0 + P*c1/(P+c2) + P*c6*exp(c7*t) + P*c8 = Candidate 41 form. MATCH.

**Candidate 15: P*c0 + P*c1/(P+c2) + P*c3*exp(c4*t) + P*c5*(1-(P*c6)^c7)^c8**

Set c5=0 → Candidate 39. MATCH.

**Candidate 22: P*c0 + P*c1/(P+c2) + P*c3*exp(c4*t) + P*c5*log(c6/(P+c7)+1)**

P*log(c6/(P+c7)+1) = P*log((P+c7+c6)/(P+c7)). This is a logarithmic function, not rational. Set c5=0 → Candidate 39. MATCH.

**Candidate 25: P*c0 + P*c1/(P+c2) + P*c3*exp(c4*t) + P^c5*c6*sin(c7*t+c8)**

Set c6=0 → Candidate 39. MATCH.

**Candidate 26: P*c0 + P*c1/(P+c2) + P*c3*log(c4/(P+c5)+1) + P^c6*c7*exp(c8*t)**

Set c6=1 for P*exp term, c8=-α. Set c3=0 → Candidate 39 form. MATCH.

**Candidate 40: P*c0 + P*c1/(P+c2) + P*c3*exp(c4*t) + c5*sin(P*c6+c7*exp(c8*t)+c9)**

Set c5=0 → Candidate 39. MATCH.

**Candidate 55: P*c0 + P*c1/(P+c2) + P*c3*exp(c4*t) + P*c5 + P*c6*sin(c7*t+c8)**

Set c6=0 → Candidate 41. MATCH.

**Candidate 19: P*c0 + P*c1/(P+c2) + P*c3*exp(c4*t)*sin(c5*t+c6) + P^c7*c8 + c9**

This has P*exp(c4*t)*sin(c5*t+c6) instead of P*exp(c4*t). Can we make sin(c5*t+c6) = 1 for all t? Only if c5=0 and c6=π/2. Then sin(c6)=1. So P*c3*exp(c4*t)*1 = c3*P*exp(c4*t). Then set c8=0, c9=0 → Candidate 39 form. MATCH.

**Candidate 21: P*c0 + P*c1/(P+c2) + P*c3*exp(c4*t)*cos(c5*t+c6) + P^c7*c8**

Similarly, set c5=0, c6=0 → cos(0)=1. Then P*c3*exp(c4*t). Set c8=0 → Candidate 39. MATCH.

Now let me check candidates with different structures:

**Candidate 31: P*c0 + P*c1*exp(c2*t) + P*c3*log(1+c4/P) + c5**

P*log(1+c4/P). Is this equivalent to P²/(aP+b)?

P*log(1+c4/P) for general P is a logarithmic function. It's NOT a rational function. For large P, P*log(1+c4/P) ≈ c4, but for finite P it has log terms. This cannot equal P²/(aP+b) which is a rational function.

So unless we can set c3=0 and c5 provides the rational term... but c5 is just a constant, not P²/(aP+b).

If c3=0: P*c0 + P*c1*exp(c2*t) + c5. This is linear in P plus exponential decay times P plus constant. GT has a nonlinear rational term in P, so this can't match.

**Candidate 31: NO MATCH.**

**Candidate 61: P*c0 + P*c1*exp(c2*t) + P*c3*log(1+c4/P)**

Same issue. P*log(1+c/P) ≠ P²/(aP+b). If c3=0, we lose the rational term. NO MATCH.

**Candidate 30: P*c0 + P*c1*exp(c2*t) + P*c3 + P*c4*log(1+c5/P) + c6**

Same as 31 with extra P*c3. Still can't produce P²/(aP+b). NO MATCH.

**Candidate 37: P*c0 + P*c1*exp(c2*t) + P*c3*log(c4/(P+c5)+1)**

P*log(c4/(P+c5)+1) = P*log((P+c5+c4)/(P+c5)). Still logarithmic, not rational. NO MATCH.

**Candidate 27: P*c0 + P*c1*exp(c2*t) + P*c3*log(1+c4/P) + P*c5*log(1+c6/P) + c7**

Two log terms can be combined: P*(c3+c5)*log(1+c'/P) if c4=c6, or P*log[(1+c4/P)^c3 * (1+c6/P)^c5]. Still logarithmic. NO MATCH.

**Candidate 7: P*c0 + P*c1*exp(c2*t) + P*c3*log(1+c4/P) + P^c5*c6*log(1+c7/P) + c8**

If c5=2: P²*c6*log(1+c7/P). This is P²*log(1+c7/P), still not rational. If c6=0, we lose it. NO MATCH.

**Candidate 9: P*c0 + P*c1*exp(c2*t) + P*c3*log(1+c4/P) + P^c5*c6 + c7**

If c3=0: P*c0 + P*c1*exp(c2*t) + P^c5*c6 + c7. We need P²/(aP+b) from P^c5*c6 + c7 + c0*P. But P^c5 is a power function, not a rational function. NO MATCH.

**Candidate 1: P*c0 + P*c1*exp(c2*t) + P*c3*log(1+c4/P) + c5 + c6*log(c7*exp(P*c8+c9*t)+1)**

The last term is a softplus-like function of P and t. Set c6=0 → Candidate 31. Still NO MATCH (same issue with log term).

Actually wait - can we set c3=0 AND use the softplus term? c6*log(c7*exp(P*c8+c9*t)+1). For this to equal P²/(aP+b), we'd need a rational function, but softplus is not rational. NO MATCH.

**Candidate 2: P*c0 + P*c1*exp(c2*t) + c3 + c4/sqrt(1+c5/P) + c6*log(c7*exp(P*c8+c9*t)+1)**

1/sqrt(1+c5/P) = sqrt(P)/sqrt(P+c5) = sqrt(P/(P+c5)). Not rational in P. Set c6=0: P*c0 + P*c1*exp(c2*t) + c3 + c4/sqrt(1+c5/P). The sqrt term can't produce P²/(aP+b). NO MATCH.

**Candidate 3: P*c0 + P*c1*exp(c2*t) + P*c3*log(1+c4/P) + c5 + c6*exp(c7*t)*log(P*c8+1)**

Set c3=0, then we need c6*exp(c7*t)*log(P*c8+1) to be time-independent and equal to P²/(aP+b). But it has exp(c7*t) multiplied by log, so setting c7=0 gives c6*log(P*c8+1), which is logarithmic, not rational. NO MATCH.

**Candidate 4: P*c0 + P*c1*exp(c2*t) + c3 + c4/sqrt(1+c5/P) + c6*exp(c7*t)*log(P*c8+1)**

Similar issues. sqrt and log terms can't produce rational function. NO MATCH.

**Candidate 5: P*c0 + P*c1*exp(c2*t) + P^c3*c4*log(P*c5+1) + c6 + c7/sqrt(1+c8/P)**

P^c3*log(P*c5+1) and 1/sqrt(1+c8/P) - neither is rational. NO MATCH.

**Candidate 8: P*c0 + P*c1*exp(c2*t) + P^c3*c4*exp(c5*t) + c6 + c7/sqrt(1+c8/P)**

P^c3*exp(c5*t): if c5=0, this is P^c3*c4, a power function. Plus 1/sqrt term. Neither produces P²/(aP+b). 

Wait - could we use both P*c1*exp(c2*t) AND P^c3*c4*exp(c5*t) together? Set c3=1, then we have two P*exp terms. Still need P²/(aP+b) from c0*P + c6 + c7/sqrt(1+c8/P). The sqrt term isn't rational. NO MATCH.

**Candidate 10: P²*c0 + P*c1 + P*c2*exp(c3*t) + P*c4 + c5 + c6/sqrt(1+c7/P)**

Has P², P, P*exp, constant, and sqrt term. P²/(aP+b) requires a rational function. P²*c0 is just a polynomial term. c0*P² + (c1+c4)*P + c5 is a polynomial, not P²/(aP+b). The sqrt term doesn't help. NO MATCH.

**Candidate 11: P*c0 + P*c1*exp(c2*t) + P*c3*log(1+c4/P) + c5*log(c6*exp(P*c7)+1)**

Log terms, not rational. NO MATCH.

**Candidate 12: P*c0 + P*c1*exp(c2*t) + c3*sin(c4*exp(P*c5+c6*t)+c7)**

Sin of exponential - highly nonlinear. If c3=0, we lose the nonlinear P term. NO MATCH.

**Candidate 13: P²*c0 + P*c1 + P*c2*exp(c3*t) + P*c4*log(1+c5/P) + P*c6 + c7**

Has P², P, P*exp, P*log(1+c/P), constant. The log term is not rational. Set c4=0: P²*c0 + (c1+c6)*P + c2*P*exp(c3*t) + c7. This is polynomial + exp term, not P²/(aP+b). NO MATCH.

**Candidate 16: P*c0 + P*c1*exp(c2*t) + P*c3*log(1+c4/P) + P*c5*(1-(P*c6)^c7)^c8 + c9**

Set c5=0 and c3=0: just P*c0 + P*c1*exp(c2*t) + c9. Missing rational term. 
Set c3=0, keep c5 term: P*c5*(1-(P*c6)^c7)^c8. This is a complicated power function. For it to equal P²/(aP+b)... unlikely to be exactly rational. NO MATCH.

**Candidate 18: P*c0 + P*c1*exp(c2*t) + P^c3*c4 + P^c5*c6*exp(c7*t)*sin(c8*t+c9)**

Set c8=0, c9=π/2: sin(π/2)=1. Then P^c5*c6*exp(c7*t). So we have two exp(t) terms: P*c1*exp(c2*t) and P^c5*c6*exp(c7*t). If c5=1, c7=c2, they combine. We still need P²/(aP+b) from P*c0 + P^c3*c4. This is c0*P + c4*P^c3, a sum of power functions, not rational. NO MATCH.

**Candidate 20: P*c0 + P*c1*exp(c2*t) + P^c3*c4 + c5*cos(c6*exp(P^c7*c8+c9*t))**

cos of exponential - highly nonlinear. Set c5=0: P*c0 + P*c1*exp(c2*t) + P^c3*c4. Power function, not rational. NO MATCH.

**Candidate 23: P*c0 + P*c1*exp(c2*t) + P*c3*log(1+c4/P) + P^c5*c6/(P^c5+c7) + c8**

P^c5*c6/(P^c5+c7): if c5=1, this is c6*P/(P+c7). Then we have P*c0 + P*c1*exp(c2*t) + P*c3*log(1+c4/P) + c6*P/(P+c7) + c8.

Set c3=0: P*c0 + P*c1*exp(c2*t) + c6*P/(P+c7) + c8. This is like Candidate 39 with a constant! 

P*c0 + c6*P/(P+c7) = same structure as before. Can this produce P²/(aP+b)?

Yes! As shown for Candidate 39, P*c0 + c6*P/(P+c7) can equal P²/(βP+1) with appropriate constants. The extra c8 can be set to 0.

So Candidate 23 with c3=0, c5=1: MATCH.

**Candidate 24: P*c0 + P*c1*exp(c2*t) + P*c3*log(1+c4/P) + c5 + c6/sqrt(1+c7/P)**

Set c3=0, c6=0: P*c0 + P*c1*exp(c2*t) + c5. Missing rational term. NO MATCH.

**Candidate 28: P*c0 + P*c1*exp(c2*t) + c3 + c4/sqrt(1+c5/P) + c6*cos(c7*exp(c8*t))**

sqrt and cos terms. Set c4=0, c6=0: P*c0 + P*c1*exp(c2*t) + c3. Missing rational term. NO MATCH.

**Candidate 29: P*c0 + P*c1*exp(c2*t) + c3*(P^c4*c5+1)^(c6*sin(c7*t+c8))**

Complex power/sin structure. If c6=0: (...)^0 = 1, so c3*1 = c3. Then P*c0 + P*c1*exp(c2*t) + c3. Missing rational term. NO MATCH.

**Candidate 32: P*c0 + P*c1*exp(c2*t) + P*c3 + c4 + c5/sqrt(1+c6/P)**

= (c0+c3)*P + c1*P*exp(c2*t) + c4 + c5/sqrt(1+c6/P). sqrt term not rational. NO MATCH.

**Candidate 33: P*c0 + P*c1*exp(c2*t) + c3*|P| + c4 + c5/sqrt(1+c6/P)**

With P≥0, |P|=P. Same as 32. NO MATCH.

**Candidate 34: P*c0 + P*c1*exp(c2*t) + c3 + c4/sqrt(1+c5/P)**

sqrt term. NO MATCH.

**Candidate 35: P*c0 + P*c1*exp(c2*t) + c3 + c4*(P^c5*c6+1)^(c7*cos(c8*t))**

If c7=0: (...)^0=1, c4*1=c4. Then linear + exp + constant. NO MATCH.

**Candidate 36: P*c0 + P*c1*exp(c2*t) + c3*(1+c4/P)^(c5*sin(c6*t+c7))**

If c5=0: (...)^0=1, c3. Same issue. NO MATCH.

**Candidate 38: P³*c0 + P²*c1 + P²*c2 + P*c3 + P*c4*exp(c5*t) + P*c6 + P*c7*log(1+c8/P) + c9**

Set c0=0, c7=0: P²*(c1+c2) + (c3+c6)*P + c4*P*exp(c5*t) + c9. This is polynomial + exp, not rational. NO MATCH.

**Candidate 42: P*c0 + P*c1*exp(c2*t) + c3*cos(c4*exp(c5/sqrt(P)))**

cos of exp - not rational. Set c3=0: missing rational term. NO MATCH.

**Candidate 43:** Similar. NO MATCH.

**Candidate 44: P*c0 + P*c1*exp(c2*t) + c3 + c4*exp(c5*t)*sin(c6*t+c7)/P**

Has 1/P term with time dependence. Set c4=0: missing rational term. NO MATCH.

**Candidate 45: P*c0 + P*c1*exp(c2*t) + P^c3*c4*exp(c5*t)*sin(c6*t+c7) + c8**

Set c6=0, c7=π/2: P^c3*c4*exp(c5*t). If c3=1, c5=c2: combines with second term. Still missing rational term. NO MATCH.

**Candidate 46: P*c0 + P*c1*exp(c2*t) + c3 + c4/sqrt(1+c5/P) + c6*exp(c7*sin(c8*t+c9))**

sqrt and exp(sin) terms. NO MATCH.

**Candidate 47: P*c0 + P*c1*exp(c2*t) + P^c3*c4*exp(c5*t) + c6*log(c7*exp(P*c8)+1)**

If c4=0 and c6=0: P*c0 + P*c1*exp(c2*t). Missing rational. 
If c3=1: two P*exp terms combine. Still need rational from c6*log(c7*exp(P*c8)+1) + c0*P. Softplus ≠ rational. NO MATCH.

**Candidate 48: P*c0 + P*c1*exp(c2*t) + P*c3*log(1+c4/P) + P^c5*c6*exp(c7*t)*cos(c8*t) + c9**

Set c8=0: P^c5*c6*exp(c7*t). If c5=1, c7=c2: combines with P*c1*exp. Set c3=0: missing rational. NO MATCH.

**Candidate 49: P*c0 + P*c1*exp(c2*t) + P^c3*c4*exp(c5*t) + c6**

If c5=0: P^c3*c4 (power function) + c0*P + c1*P*exp + c6. Power function ≠ rational. NO MATCH.

Actually wait - what if we use BOTH exp terms? c1*P*exp(c2*t) + c4*P^c3*exp(c5*t). If c3=1: (c1*exp(c2*t) + c4*exp(c5*t))*P. This gives us the P*exp(-αt) part if c2=c5=-α (they combine). But then we still need P²/(aP+b) from c0*P + c6, which is just linear. NO MATCH.

**Candidate 50: P*c0 + P*c1*exp(c2*t) + c3 + c4/sqrt(1+c5/P) + c6*exp(c7*t)*sin(c8*t+c9)**

Set c4=0, c6=0: linear + exp + constant. NO MATCH.

**Candidate 51: P*c0 + P*c1*exp(c2*t) + P*c3*log(1+c4/P) + P*c5 + P*c6*sin(c7*t+c8) + c9**

Set c6=0, c3=0: (c0+c5)*P + c1*P*exp + c9. NO MATCH.

**Candidate 52: P*c0 + P*c1*exp(c2*t) + P*c3*sin(c4*t+c5) + c6 + c7/sqrt(1+c8/P)**

Set c3=0, c7=0: linear + exp + constant. NO MATCH.

**Candidate 53:** Similar with sin and sqrt. NO MATCH.

**Candidate 54: P*c0 + P*c1*exp(c2*t) + P*c3*log(1+c4/P) + P*c5*sin(c6*t+c7) + c8**

Set c5=0, c3=0: linear + exp + constant. NO MATCH.

**Candidate 56:** log and cos of exp terms. NO MATCH.

**Candidate 57: P*c0 + P*c1*exp(c2*t) + P^c3*c4*exp(c5*t) + c6*log(P*c7+1)/P**

log(P)/P term - not rational in the right way. NO MATCH.

**Candidate 58:** sin of log - not rational. NO MATCH.

**Candidate 59: P^(1/3)*c0 + P*c1 + P*c2*exp(c3*t) + P*c4*log(1+c5/P)**

Set c0=0, c4=0: P*c1 + P*c2*exp(c3*t). Missing rational. NO MATCH.

Now let me compile the matches:

Candidates that match: 6, 14, 15, 17, 19, 21, 22, 23, 25, 26, 39, 40, 41, 55, 60

Wait, let me double-check some of these more carefully.

**Candidate 22: P*c0 + P*c1/(P+c2) + P*c3*exp(c4*t) + P*c5*log(c6/(P+c7)+1)**

Set c5=0: P*c0 + P*c1/(P+c2) + P*c3*exp(c4*t) = Candidate 39. MATCH ✓

**Candidate 23 re-check:** With c5=1, c3=0: P*c0 + P*c1*exp(c2*t) + c6*P/(P+c7) + c8. This is P*(c0) + c6*P/(P+c7) + P*c1*exp(c2*t) + c8. Same as Candidate 39 + constant c8 (set c8=0). MATCH ✓

**Candidate 26 re-check:** P*c0 + P*c1/(P+c2) + P*c3*log(c4/(P+c5)+1) + P^c6*c7*exp(c8*t)

Set c3=0: P*c0 + P*c1/(P+c2) + P^c6*c7*exp(c8*t). Set c6=1: P*c0 + P*c1/(P+c2) + c7*P*exp(c8*t) = Candidate 39. MATCH ✓

Let me verify all the "P*c1/(P+c2)" candidates more carefully to make sure I haven't missed any issues.

The key insight is: P*a + b*P/(P+d) with appropriate a, b, d can produce P²/(eP+f).

Common denominator: [a*P*(P+d) + b*P]/(P+d) = P[aP + ad + b]/(P+d)

For this to equal g*P²/(eP+f), we need:
P(aP + ad + b)/(P+d) = gP²/(eP+f)

So (aP + ad + b)/(P+d) = gP/(eP+f)

Cross multiply: (aP + ad + b)(eP+f) = gP(P+d)

Left: aeP² + afP + adeP + adf + beP + bf = aeP² + (af + ade + be)P + adf + bf
Right: gP² + gdP

Matching:
- P²: ae = g
- P: af + ade + be = gd
- constant: adf + bf = 0 → f(ad + b) = 0

So either f=0 or ad+b=0.

If f=0: P²/(eP) = P/e, which is just linear. Not what we want.
If ad+b=0, i.e., b=-ad:

Then from P²: ae = g
From P: af + ade + be = gd → af + ade - ade = gd → af = gd → f = gd/a = aed/a = ed

So f = ed, meaning eP+f = e(P+d).

Then g*P²/(eP+f) = ae*P²/(e(P+d)) = a*P²/(P+d).

So P*a + (-ad)*P/(P+d) = a*P - ad*P/(P+d) = aP[1 - d/(P+d)] = aP*P/(P+d) = a*P²/(P+d).

GT: 0.3156*P²/(9.871P+1) = 0.3156*P²/(9.871(P+1/9.871)) = (0.3156/9.871)*P²/(P+0.1013)

So a = 0.3156/9.871 = 0.03197, d = 0.1013.
b = -ad = -0.03197*0.1013 = -0.003239.

This confirms the calculation. ✓

Now let me also reconsider some candidates I might have dismissed too quickly.

**Candidate 49: P*c0 + P*c1*exp(c2*t) + P^c3*c4*exp(c5*t) + c6**

Could we set c3=2, c5=0? Then P²*c4 + c0*P + c1*P*exp(c2*t) + c6. This is a polynomial in P (quadratic) plus exp term plus constant. But GT has P²/(aP+b), a rational function, not P². NO MATCH confirmed.

**Candidate 8: P*c0 + P*c1*exp(c2*t) + P^c3*c4*exp(c5*t) + c6 + c7/sqrt(1+c8/P)**

Even with two exp terms combining, we need P²/(aP+b) from remaining terms. sqrt term can't provide this. NO MATCH confirmed.

**Candidate 45:** Set c6=0, c7=π/2 → sin=1. P^c3*c4*exp(c5*t) + c0*P + c1*P*exp(c2*t) + c8. If c3≠1, we get a power*exp term. Can't produce rational function. NO MATCH.

Let me reconsider **Candidate 18**: P*c0 + P*c1*exp(c2*t) + P^c3*c4 + P^c5*c6*exp(c7*t)*sin(c8*t+c9)

Set c8=0, c9=π/2 → sin=1: P*c0 + P*c1*exp(c2*t) + P^c3*c4 + P^c5*c6*exp(c7*t)

If c5=1, c7=c2: P*c0 + (c1+c6)*P*exp(c2*t) + P^c3*c4. Still need P²/(aP+b) from c0*P + P^c3*c4. This is c0*P + c4*P^c3, which is a sum of power functions. Not rational. NO MATCH confirmed.
